Comment

This file contains scanned images of a Well Report submitted under
Australian Government legislation . The data in this file are made available to
assist future explorers for petroleum and may be distributed freely .

Please refer any queries to

-----Page 30-----

2.0 OPERATIONAL SUMMARY

-----Page 31-----

2.0 OPERATIONAL SUMMARY WELL : NANCAR 1

The rig arrived at location at 1430 hours 16th April 1989 .
Anchors were run and pretensioned . The rig was then
secured for a cyclone alert and waited on weather for three
days . The rig was then moved 700m due to a change in
locatlon and anchors rerun .

The 36 hole was spudded in at 0245 hours 24th April 1989
and drilled to 316m . The 30 casing was run and set at Jlim .

The 26 hole was drilled to 717m . The 20 casing was run and
cemented at 707m . The BOP stack and riser were then run and
tested .

The 17.5 hole was drilled down to 1665m where Losses were

encountered . Drilling continued to 2030m with intermittent
losses . The hole was logged and 13.375 casing was run and

cemented at 2020m .

The 13.375 casing was drilled out and an LOT carried out
to 1.54SG . The 12.25 hole was drilled to 3019m where a
tong die was lost on a trip . After recovering the die
drilling continued to 3308m . Two 8.5 cores were then
cut to 3326m . After reaming the core holes drilling
continued to 3434m where the BHA became stuck after a
bit trip . The BHA above the first string stabiliser was
backed off at 3326m and the three attempts made to fish
the assembly were unsuccessful .

One logging run was made and the sidetrack plug set from
3260m to 3106m . The well was then sidetracked in 12.25
from 3115m to 3650m . After running logs the well was
plugged and abandoned . The rig was off location at

1300 hours on the last of July 1989 .

3.0 MUD SUMMARY BY HOLE SECTION WELL : NANCAR 1

36 HOLE 254m TO 316m

The 36 hole section was drilled with seawater and HiVis
( Kwikthik ) mud sweeps pumped every connection and half
kelly . The hole was flushed with 200bb1 of HiVis mud and
the hole displaced with HiVis mud prior to running 30
casing to 3llm . Good returns were observed at seabed during
cementing operations .

26 HOLE 316m TO 717m 20 CASING AT 708m

The 26 hole section was drilled with seawater and 50bbl
Hivis ( Flocculated Kwikthik ) mud sweeps every connection and
at half kelly down To maintain e clean hole the hole was
swept with 100bbl1s HiVis on every third or fourth kelly .

At TD the hole was swept with 150bbls HiVis mud followed by
600bbls seawater then another 150bbls HiVis mud followed
by 900bbl1ls seawater . The hole was displaced with 1100bbls
of HiVis mud including 300bb1s of non focculated Kwikthik
mud on bottom . The 20 casing was run and cemented without
problems at 707m .

17.5 HOLE 717m TO 2030m 13.375 CASING AT 2020m

The 20 casing was drilled out with seawater dumping the
returns . A closed seewater gel mud system was displaced
with full returns at 730n . The hole was drilled to 1291m
where a bit change was made . Mud Weight was controlled at
1.08 SG maximum and Rheology ( YP 20131b100ft2 ) and API
Fluid Loss ( 24m144m1 ) were loosely controlled by additions
of prehydrated Kwikthik and seawater . On POOH an overpull
of 50.0001bs maximum was recorded between 1183m and 1154m . A
wiper trip at 1626m showed no drag or fill . A drilling
break occurred at 1662m and static losses were monitored

( at 1665m ) at 25bblhr . Total losses occurred at 171lin .

The autofill valve was opened and no returns were observed
while pumping . POOH to 1430m and conditioned the mud
observed losses . The hole was drilled to 1719m ( past the
fractureloss zone ) with losses of 160300bblhr . A LCM .
pill was spotted ( 1lppb Kwikseal Nutplug ) . Pulled back to
1424m with losses of 300bblhr . Drilling continued to 1741m
without losses . Total losses again occurred

( as anticipated ) when the roller reamer passed the loss zone
at 1714m . After drilling several more metres to 1743m the
bit was pulled up to 1710m and another LCM pill ( 13ppb
Kwikseel ) was spotted . Pulled to 1433m with losses of
300bblshr . Opened the autofill valve and spotted another
LCM pill above the loss zone at 1682m . Pulled to 1596n
closed the autofill valve and then drilled from 1743n to
1770n with losses increasing up to 110bblhr . Mud weight
was being maintained as low as possible ( 1.06 1.08 Sa )
Yield Point at over 201b100ft2 and Fluid Loss was less
than 10m130min . The previous procedure was again repeated
an LCM p111 ( 15ppb Kwikseal r Nutplug ) was spotted a small
trip made and on running in hole drilling continued . The

-----Page 62-----

3.0 MUD SUMMARY BY HOLE SECTION WELL : NANCAR 1

hole was drilled to 1854m maintaining full returns . A
drilling break was observed at 1842m . Losses of 60bblhr
were observed from 1921.5m ( 19271981m 80X sandstone ) .
Calcium Carbonate ( bridging agent ) pills ( mud 20ppb CaC03
10ppb dry gel ) were spotted et 1927m at 1973m at 1986m
and at 1988m . Drilling continued to 2015m ( 90954
claystone ) where losses ( 60bblhr ) were treated with a 50bbl
LCM ( Kwikseal ) pill . Drilled to section TD at 2030m without
problems . XCD Polymer had been added to maintain Yield
Point above 201b100ft2 .

At 2030m a LCM pill was apotted fron 1718m to 1668m a CaC03
pill from 1925m to 1875m . 4102 KCI mud was spotted from
2030m to 1980m prior to pulling out of the hole for logging
After logging the hole was circulated clean on a wiper trip .
50bb1 KC1 mud was spotted on bottom prior to running

casing . The hole was found to be generally overgauge from
707m to 750m ( 1623 ) within an inch of gauge from 750m to
1930m ( 16.518.5 ) and from 1930m to 2010m slightly
overgauge ( 1819 ) . 13.375 casing was run and cemented at
2020p without problems ( total losses 90bbls ) .

12.25 HOLE 2030m3434m

The 13.375 cesing cement was drilled from 1991m with mud
salvaged from the previous interval pretreated with
Bicarbonate for Calcium ( cement ) contamination . A FIT test
was performed at 2034m to an Equivalent Mud Weight of

1.54 Sa .

The mud system was converted to a KC1 Polyacrylamide
( Polyplus ) system by 2100m . The MBT was reduced the KC1
concentration raised to over 85 and 2.5ppb ( 324 ) Polyplus
added . The Yield Point at 13201b100ft2 was raised to
241b100ft2 by 3000m . The Mud Weight was raised from 1.105G
to 1.15 SO by 23125 .

A trip at 2142m ( for a suspected wash out ) showed no drag or
fill . KCI1 concentration dropped to 5X at 2200m due to
supply shortages and was raised to 8X again by 3000m . The
Mud Weight was raised to 1.17 SG by 2788m raised to 1.20 SG
at 2899m and after a trip at 2959m to 1.22 SG . Some shale
cavings were observed at the shale shakers and high
maintenance of pH ( 52 x 25kg KOH used from 2312m to 2899n )
indicated acid gas ( C02 H2SCO2 considered likely ) .

Raising the Mud Weight reduced the alkali consumption
stabilising pH .

Cores were cut from 3308m . Core # 1 3308m to 3313m . Core # 2
3313m to 3327m . Yield Point was kept at 251b100ft2 min
whilst coring .

Drilling continued to 3434m . Mud Weight had been raised to
1.25 SG . Pipe got stuck on running into the ( gauge ) hole
with the new BHA and bit . A 15bbl pill of Macolube and

-----Page 63-----

3.0 MUD SUMMARY BY HOLE SECTION WELL : NANCAR 1

PipeLax wes spotted but the pipe could not be freed . A
caustic pill was pumped but again the pipe could not be
freed and eventually was backed off . The remaining pipe
could not be fished successfully so the hole was plugged
back . A cement plug was set from 3260m to 3106m .

12.25 HOLE SIDETRACK 3106m 3650m

The cement was tagged at 3106m . Kickoff point for sidetrack
was at 3115m . Drilling then continued to 3474m without

any hole problems . Mud welght was maintained at 1.25 SG
Yield Point at 22251b100ft2 API Fluid Loss 6m130nin
HTHP less than 20m130min . pH which had increased from

the cement to 11 was reduced to 9.5 by 3365m . KCL
concentration was maintained at over 8.04 and Polyacrylamide
concentration was maintained and edditions adjusted to
penetratlon rates which were at times reduced to Imhr .

Trips were made at 3247m 3307m 3365m 3418m 3454m and
3474m without any hole problems . A wiper trip at 3469m
encountered overpull at 3456m ( 1400001b ) and on running in
the hole at 3474m the section 3412m3467m was washed and
reamed . Some drag was experienced ( at 3421m ) on a wiper
trip at 3565m and trips at 3593m and 3600m were made
without problems .

Drilling continued ( often at rates of 12mhr ) to 3650m RKB
TD . ( Mud Weight which did rise to 1.26 SG was maintained at
1.25 SG . Biozan was added to maintain the Yield Point
instead of XCD . Polymer .

At TD the hole was logged and found to be mostly close to
gauge ( gauge 12.25 x 1314 16 at 2760m and 12.25 x 19
at 3173m ) . After logging the hole was plugged and abandoned .

3.0

FORMATION SAMPLING

31

Ditch Curti

Ditch cuttings were first collected from the shaker screens within the 17.5 hole .
They werc collected at 10 m intervals from 717 mKB to 2030 mKB . Within the 17.5
hole returns were lost over the interval 16951714 mKB due to lost circulation .
Cuttings are unavailable for this interval .

Ditch cuttings were collected at 3 m intervals within the 12 14 hole from 2030
mKB to 3650 mKB ( total depth ) . No intervals of lost circulation lcading to loss of
returns were encountered in this hole section .

Over the cored interval 3308 to 3326.34 mKB complete samples were not obtained
due to poor volume and quality of ditch cuttings .

Circulation times were periodically checked with carbideacetylenc gas samples and
pump stroke counters . Calculatcd lag times were adjusted accordingly .

Table No . 1 on the following page represents the sampling programme used in the
drilling of Nancar11ST . Washed and dried cuttings samples werc prepared in six
samples as detailed in Table No . 1 .

A summarized description ol the cuttings samples from Nancar11ST follows after
Table No . 1 .

FINAL DATA REPORT CONVENTIONAL CORE ANALYSIS
WELL : NANCAR # 1

A total of 18.34m of core was collected from the Lloyds Hangar at
Darwin Airport in two trips between 21st May and 22nd May 1989 .
This comprised of two continuous 4 diameter cores over the
following intervals :

Core # 1 3308.00 3313.26m
Core # 2 3313.26 3326.34m

Upon arrival at the Core Services laboratory a continuous core
gamma was run and on completion of this the core was removed from
its synthetic inner barrel one metre at a time lald out orlented

as to dip and marked for depth .

Two plug samples were chosen at each 30cm interval astride a fluid
saturation sample . One plug was cut parallel to the bedding plane
and the second across the bedding plane at 90 to the first thus
giving theoretical maximum and minimum permeabllity into the well
bore . Nine full diameter samples were selected at approximately two
metre intervals taking into account best representation of the
hetrogeneous sectlons of the core . All sections of the core were
represented by plug analysis . This required mounting of twentytwo
samples .

The following report includes tabular data : a continuous core gamma
log : a corelog plot and a permeability vs porosity plot .

The data contained in this report has been derived by the following
methods :

L. CONTINUOUS CORE GAMMA : ls produced by passing the
whole core under a gamma radlation detector shlelded
inside a lead tunnel on a continuous belt . The
continuous belt ls driven at an adjustable speed
designed to reproduce the desired vertical log scale .
The gamma radiation count is amplified and the signal
digltized to reflect the drawn log .

contdpage # 2

-----Page 138-----

SUMMATION OF FLUID POROSITY : determined by the
additlon of connate water and oll from the retort
together with the gas occupled space determined by
mercury Injectlon .

FLUID SATURATIONS : An automatic thermostatically
controlled high temperature retort was utilized for the
volumetric determinations of connate water and residual
oil saturatlons .

NATURAL DENSITY : derlved by measurements utilizing a
Boyles Law displacement pump to determine bulk volume
and an analytical balance to determine the wet weight .

PERMEABILITY : Measured by Fluld Transmissibility
Darcys Equation for compressible flulds ( gas ) assuming
the lamina flow ls the theory on which used .

HELIUM INJECTION POROSITY : Measured by helium
porosimeter to determine the grain volume and
consequently pore volume . This porosity determination
is based on the Boyles Law Equation and uses the helium
because of its minute molecular structure and inert
propertles .

GRAIN DENSITY : Derived by measurements utilizing a
Boyles Law displacement pump to determine bulk volume
and an analytical balance to determine weight .

OVERBURDEN STRESS TESTS : Permeability and Porosity
are measured as in ( 5 ) and ( 6 ) aboveutllizing a high
pressure chamber inside of which the sample is enclosed
in a neoprene sheath surrounded by a noncompressible
liquid . Pressure ls exerted on the sample via the
Uquid sufficient to simulate the overburden stress

in a triaxlal mode . Appropriate pressures were
supplled by the cllent

CORE FULL DIAMETER TESTS : Porosity the method
detailed in ( 6 ) above is utlllzed . The sample size is
full dlameter and normally 20 26cm in length .
Permeability same method as in ( 5 ) above ls used
however permeablllty is measured in three distinct
directlons

( a ) Maximum horizontal permeability is found .

( b ) Permeability measurement ls made at 90 deg .
to the maximum and a vertical permeabllity
is determined .

All three permeabilities are measured utilizing a

sample of full diameter core .

-----Page 139-----

10 . BRINELL HARDNESS TESTS : Flve points in a cross
pattern are selected at each sample Interval as the
load point for a 3.176mm indentor . A preload of 10kg
and a constant load of 20kg are utilized to provide the
indentation which ts then measured for depth . Data
from the flve points 1s averaged and utilized in the
standard B.H.N . formula . The minimum attainable
Brinell Hardness reading is 4 .

11 . A.P.I . GRAVITY : Composite sample from a particular
reservoir ls collected from the retort during fluid
saturation determinatlons . Specific gravity Is
measured by the pycnometer method and converted
mathimatlcally to degrees A.P.I . to comply with
Industry standards .

12 . ROLLING AVERAGES 4 SPECIFIED AVERAGES : Please refer
to explanations and formulae overleaf .

112 plugs were drilled for helium injectlon porosity horizontal
permeability and grain density determinations . The majority of the
plugs were drilled with compressed air as the lubricating medium
while the remainder were drilled utilizing water . The plugs were
then cleaned with toluene in soxhlet extractors . The cycled toluene
was checked for density comparison with clean toluene as a control
to ensure no extractable oll remained in the plugs . After cleaning
the plugs were drled in a controlled humidity environment at
temperatures not exceedlng 105 degrees centlgrade . The plugs then
attained room temperature in a vacuum desslcator charged with silica
gel prior to analysis . Fluid saturation samples were trimmed out
with a diamond saw utilizing compressed air as the lubricatlng
medium to minimize damage from the use of core hammers .

On completion of the analysis the core was slabbed Into one half
and two quarter slabs using water and compressed alr as the
lubricating medium . One quarter was packed and shipped to the
N.T.M.D . The remaining quarter was packed and shipped to the B.M.R .
Canberra . The one half slab was photographed under both white light
and vitraviolet light . This half was then packed and shipped to
the BHPP Core Store in Melbourne .

Should you have any queries regarding this data please do not
hesitate to contact us .

We have enjoyed working with BHPP and look forward to working with
you again in the near future .

END OF REPORT

-----Page 140-----

DESCRIPTICN OF PLUG CUITING :

R PLUGS : ( regular plugs ) cut in the horizontal plane along the strike of the
bedding to give theoretical maximum permeability into the well bore .
NA PLUGS : cut in the horizontal plane at 90 to the Rplugs and across the

bedding to give a theoretical minimum permeability of the formation
into the well bore .

NY ! PLUGS : cut in the vertical plane of the core .

ROLLING AVERAGES :

These averages of both Heliun injection porosity and permeability are obtained by
using a rolling three ( 3 ) point method . In the case of porosity a weighted arithmetic
average is used .

Bania1 ) 3 bj 1 2D ( i4 ) 46 ( i4 YI4
In the case of permability a weighted geometric average is used
Kang a 3 210 LQ9Bj Kat 2logto NG a 1 ) ? logto Kis ? ) 14
At any sanple point excluding the first and last a rolling average is obtained by using
the value at the specified sanple point . The valve preceeding it and the value of the

sample poinc subsequent to it . In the cases of the first and last sample points only 2
sample points were used .

Using porosity as an example the average of the first data point is obcained from che
formula .

Bang ) 205404 913
The average at the final data point is obtained by :

The same method is used for permeability averages . At any break in the data the rolling

-----Page 177-----

Mudlogging Unit

Geoservices Overseas S.A. provided conventional mudlogging
services in conjunction with a computerised data logging and
processing system ( Advanced Logging System ) .

Gas detection equipment consisted of :

Flame Ionization Total Hydrocarbon Ditch Gas Detector .

Flame Ionization Chromatograph ( continuous
cyclehydrocarbon detection C through to C ) .

Blender Gas detector ( for gas analysis of drill
cuttings ) .

Hydrogen Sulphide detector ( continuous monitoring
sensitive to 1 ppa ) .

The Geoservices Advanced Logging System fully utilised to
measure display and record conventional drilling data . A
visual display of current drilling parameters was continuously
updated on a 5 second scan . Permanent storage of drilling data
was recorded onto 5 IBM compatible disks . 0Offline plots of
engineering data plus online printouts of selected
drilling parameters were made available when necessary .

Surveillance for potential abnormal pressure while drilling
was assisted by the continuous computation of the Dexponent .

The Geoservices unit was operated continuously throughout the
well . ( Once returns were achieved routine analyses for
fluorescence and cut in organic solvent were carried out on
s11 Gitch samples and sidewall cores .

The Mudlog for the well is included as Enclosure No . 1 .

-----Page 178-----



-----Page 179-----

42 . Wirgline Logs

Three Suites of wireline logs were run in open hole on Nancar11ST . Suite 1 was run in the 17.5 section of open hole
Nancar1 . Suite 2 was run in the 12 14 section of open hole above the fish just prior to setting the abandonment plug
for Nancar1 . Suite 3 was the TD Suite of logs and it was run in the 12 14 section of open hole NancarIST .

-----Page 181-----

43

Yelocity Survey

Seismograph Service Ltd ( SSL ) conducted two static rig source Vertical Seismic Profiles ( VSPs ) in
Nancar11ST on the 070589 and 260689 . The source for both surveys was an 80 cu . in . bolt
airgun operating at a constant pressure of 1800 psi .

The first survey ( 070589 ) was run prior to L3 38 casing with check shots taken at 20m intervals
between 2000m and 1500m below KB and at 50m intervals between 1500m and 600m below KB . An
additional level at 1393m was also used .

The second survey ( 260689 ) was run at T.D . with check shots taken at 20m intervals between
3640m and 1960m below KB . Additional levels at 1600m and 800m were also used .

A summary of the surveys including an Interval Velocity Curve Time Depth Curve and a listing of
the Calibrated Velocity Log Data is presented on the following pages .

A Velocity Log at 1:500 scale is included as Enclosure 2 .

DESCRIPTION OF SHIFTS USED IN WELOCITY LOG CALIBRATION

THO TYPES OF SHIFT MAY BE APPLIED :
( 1 ) SHIFTS TO LOHER VELOCITIES WHICH ARE APPLIED LINEARLY .
THESE SHIFTS ARE CALCULATED USING THE FORMULA 1

T TE 2 ( Th TX
Z8 21

x 103

WHERE TL AND TC ARE THE TRAVEL TIMES TO A GIVEN CHECK LEVEL
MEASURED FROM THE VELOCITY LOG AND WELL GEOPHONE DATA RESPECTIVELY
AND WHERE Z 1S THE DEPTH OF THE CHECK LEVEL BELOW DATUN .

CTL TC ) IS EXPRESSED IN MS ( AS JN THE CALIBRATION CURUE ) AND THE
RESULTING LINEAR SHIFT IS EXPRESSED IN ( JUSFT .

( 2 ) SHIFTS TO HIGHER VELOCITIES WHICH ARE APPLIED DIFFERENT IALLY

IN ORDER TO APPLY LARGER CORRECTIONS TO LOHER VELOCITY SECTIONS OF LOG .
THIS 1S BASED ON THE ASSUMPTION THAT LOWER VELOCITY SECTIONS

OF LOG CONTRIBUTE MORE TRANSIT TIME ERRORS THAN HIGHER VUELOCITY
SECTIONS DUE TO CAVING AND OTHER BOREHOLE EFFECTS .

ADDITIONALLY THIS TYPE OF SHIFT MAY BE RESTRICTED BY DEFINING A
BASELINE VALUE SUCH THAT SECTIONS OF LOG RECORDED AT A HIGHER

VELOCITY THAN THAT OF THE BASELINE HILL RECEIVE NG SHIFT .

RESTRICTED DIFFERENTIAL SHIFTS ( UNRESTRICTED SHIFTS HILL HAVE
A BASELINE VALUE OF ZERO ) ARE CALCULATED USING THE FORMULA 3

( TCz 7 Toy ) ( Z2 21 ) X BASELINE VALLE X 1085 x noox
aa ga Gay 1
Tha IL ? ( Za 24 ) X BASEL INE VALUE Xx 1075

WHERE TC AND TL ARE EXPRESSED IN SECONDS AND THE BASEL INE VALUE
IS EXPRESSED IN ( JISFT .

44

Teleco M While : Drilling

Telecos Measurement While Drilling ( MWD ) services were utilized by BHP Petroleum during the
drilling of Nancar1 and Nancar1 Sidetrack .

Realtime Gamma Ray and Resistivity logs along with Directional Surveys were recorded within the
12 14 hole below the 13 38 casing shoe which was set at 2020mKB .

In Nancar1 MWD measurements were recorded from 2020m to 3434mKB . While running back into
the hole at 3434m during a bit trip the BHA became stuck and Nancar1 was plugged and
abandoned .

Nancar1 Sidetrack was commenced with the help of the MWD tool ( Directional Surveys ) and once
the hole was safely past the fish the Teleco tool was layed down . This occurred at 3369m .

Teleco reports summarizing the MWD for both Nancar1 and Nancar1 Sidetrack can be found on
the following pages .

3 . R ING AN INEERIN

Following is an summary for sach Teleco run in each saction of
hole .

12147 Hi 02Qm 34354m

TELECO Run # 1 : OHB 281092 ( 2021m 2084m )

The 13 38 shoe was set 2020m . A slick J214 drilling
assembly was picked up and RIH drilling the cament shoe and
Formation from 2021m to 2084m . After complating a Formation
Integrity Test the mud system was changed over to KC polymer
and drilling continued to 2084m Three surveys were taken on
this run the final survey taken at a depth of 2076m having an
inclination of 0.7 deg and an azimuth of 207.9 dag . The drilling
parameters for this run were as follows WOB 29 42 RPM 48 Yi
flow 971 633 gpm and SPP of 2465 2852 psi providing a ROP af
5 10 mhr .

TELECO Run # 2 : DHB 2610 02 ( 2Q94n 2142m )

After changing tha bit to a HYCALOG D5 34 dressed
with 4 x 16 jets drilling resumed with a significantly Faster ROP
of between 15 25 mhr . Drilling parameters usad were WOB 9 12
klbs RPM 100 106 and SPP of 2920 2970 psi giving a flow of

800 810 gpm . At a depth of 225m a pressure drop of 300
400psi was experienced . Tha surface equipment was inspected and
two pump valves subsequently changed . However the pressure

fluctuations continued with a drop in pressure coincidental with
a drop in torque . Ataer the pump valves ware changed tha TELECO
tool stopped transmitting valid data .. Inspection of tha tool
diagnostics revealed that the tool was transmitting data in the
wrong mode while the tool pulse itself was very clean A survey
was attempted at the next connection but valid results were not
abtained . At this stage the FSE informed the company man that
problems were being experienced with tha tool which Were
coincidantal with the pressure fluctuations . Further inspection
of the surface equipment revealed that it was in perfect working
order and consequently the decision was made to POH and laok for
a washout . Only one survey was taken on this run giving an
inclination of O7 deg . and an azimuth of 216.5 deg . The tool
was tested at surface with no improvement in the data trans
mitted and was conssquently layed doun .

-----Page 226-----

TELECO RUN # 3 : DHB 275 10 ( 2142m 2948m )

A new tool was picked up and surface tested . The problem
experienced on the previous run was duplicated as wera the
pressure fluctuations . Despite this tha decision was made to
RIH pressurs testing each stand of BHA and every five stands of
drill pipe . Tha TELECO tool was tested again at the casing shoe
and it was found to be operational . Later it was suspactad that
the mud was spottad with sections of extremely high viscosity and
this was the cause of both the tool and pressure problans .

Drilling resumed with a average drill rate of 15 meters
an hour until 2702 meters when the WOB was increased from 13 I16
klbs to 18 22 klbs . After the increases in the WOB the drilling
rate increased to averags of 25 meters an hour . At around 2855m
the ROP decraased to 10 mhr and the decision was made to POH at
2948m . Tha inclination values for this run varied from 0.4 to
0.9 deg . while the azimuth varied Prom 63.0 deg . to 340.0 dag .
The final survay taken at a depth of 2940m . giving an
inclination of 0.5 dag . and azimuth of 93.2 dag .

TELECO RUN 4 4 : DHB 275 1Q ( 2948 3015m )

The decision was made to drill with a standard tricone
bit while very hard claystone remained the predominant Llithology
encountered since the PDC bit used on the previous run suffered
severe wear drilling this formation type . Drilling parametars
used during this run were WOB 25 45 klbs RPM 105 l1Q SPP
2350 2860 psi giving a flow rate af 550 610 gpm and an ROP
oP 3 5S mhr . There was a marked change in formation at 2998m .
with the lithology grading Prom claystona into shale . In addition
the drilling become a lot smoother at this point . Conseguently it
was decided to POH and change tha bit back to a PDC type as
outlined above . Only one survey was taken on this run at a depth
af 3003m . giving an inclination of 0.6 dag and an azimuth of
138.2 deg . Tha bit was graded at surface and found to ba in
excellent condition this was attributed to tha use of a shock
sub .

TELECO RUN # S5 : DHB 275 10 ( 3016 3019m )

After a successful surface test tha new BHA was RIH
however during tha trip in a tong jaw was lost down hole . As a
result the assembly was pulled cut the bit changed and a junk
sub added . The bottom was tagged and the pipe surged far junk .
A survey was taken off bottom giving an inclination of 0.6 deg
end an azimutn of 115.7 deg . Two metres were drilled before
pulling out . The tong jaw was recovered .

-----Page 227-----

TELECO RIN # 6 : OHB 275 10 ( 3018 3278m )

The BHA was made up incorporating the POC bit as before
and the tool succesfully surface tasted . Orilling resumed at
3018m at a rate of 16 25 mhr . This rate was maintained until
around 5255m . At this point the lithology became signiFficantly
harder and possible sand stringers were encountered reducing the
ROP to around 5 mhr . Qrilling parameters used during this run
were as follows WOB 20 24 kibs RPM Bb 110 and a SPP of
2959 29AB psi producing a flow of 710 740 gpm . From 3045
3245m the lithology encountered was axtremely homogenous and
possibiy siliceous . This resulted in a large apparent
resistivity Ct Ra I.4 .5 ohnmm . 3 ) with a very Flat
charactaristic over the interval . In addition a very low mud
resistivity resulted in a very large correction factor and
consaquently the corrected resistivity values are not
quantitative . However it should be stressed that the apparant
resistivity values that is the raw data measured by the tool is
valid and that the tool was working perfectly over this interval .
There wers several surveys taken over this section the
inclination varying from 0.7 1.6 deg and the azimuth from 163.2
200.5 deg . the final survey at 3270.5m having an inelination
of .6 dag . and an azimuth of 200.5 deg . The gamma ray dropped
significantly at 3269m indicating the top of the gand and
consequently the core point was set 3Sm into the sand at 3305m .
The lack of progress with the PCD bit in the sandier formation
resulted in the bit being pulled at 3278m .

TELECO RUN # 7 : DHB 275 10 ( 3278 3305m )

A three cone bit and shock sub were added to the
assembly to drill to the core point . Drilling parameters used
during this run were WO0OB 1444 kibs RPM of 67106 a flow of
608629 gpm and a SPP of 26482980 psi giving a ROP of 21Q mhr .
As expected the lithology encountered consisted of Interbedded
clay and sandstone . The proposed core depth of 3305m was reached
and a survey taken giving an inclination of .8 dag . and an
azimuth of 128.4 deg . After circulating bottoms up tha bit was
pulled and replaced with a core assembly .

-----Page 228-----

TELECO AUN # 8 : DHB 2071 05 ( 3308 3329.5m )

Due to the high hours on the previous TELECO tool a new
tool was picked up for thls run.The Security bit previously used
to surge for junk ( Run No 15 ) was used to open the hole from 8
t2 to 2 14 after the coring runs . It was noted at the start
of this run ( 3308m ) thara was s high static B.H . tamperature of
102 deg C. At 331Qm the tool stopped pulsing and at the same
time the SPP increased marksdly . The entire run was
characterisad by fluctuations in SPP and after a sharp increase
in 5PP the tool resumad operation briefly . At this point it was
noted that the mud was extramely aerated and that this was the
probable cause of the pressure fluctuations . In addition it
appeared that as long as the 5PP was maintained above 2400 psi
the too ! would function normally . This snhanced the belie ? that
the high degree of mud aeration was causing the loss of signal
integrity at surface . Howaver at a depth of 3322m the tool
stopped working and could not be restarted daspite working the
pipe and cycling the pumps . Drilling parameters used Far this
run were as follows WOB 24 43 klbs RPM 94 98 and a SPP of
2214 2747 giving a flow of 640 649 gpm . Only one survey was
taken during this run at a depth of 3298m having an inclination
cf 1.8 deg and an azimuth of 193.1 . After drilling new formation
for 2m in order to gauge drilling conditions for the next run the
decision Was mada to pull cut .

TELECO RUN # 9 DHB 275 10 ( 3329m 3389m )

Tne faulty tool B270105 was laid down and the previous
tool B27S 10 was picked up and run in the hole after surface

testing . The formation data over the cored hola section was
obtained by reaming before drilling commenced at 3328m . The
predominant lithology encountered was a soft claystone with very
hard sandstone being drilled over the last 0m . Orilling was

very slow over this section with the ROP averaging 1.5 mhr . It
was decided to pull out at 3399n as the bit was not suited to the

formation type . ODrilling parameters for this run were as
Follows WOB 31 57 klb RPM 4G 6Q @ flow 572 592 gpm and SPP
of 2805 2664 psi . The inclination values for this section

ranged from 1.8 2. deg . and the azimuth from 61.6 358.0
deg the # lnal survey at a depth of 3375m having an inclination
af 1.8 seg and an azimuth of 358.0 deg .

-----Page 229-----

TELECO RUN # 10 DHB 275 1G ( 33B9m 3400m )

Drilling resumed with a REED HP31 ! bit at 3389m without any
improvement in the ROP which remainad at 2 mhr as it had
over the previous section . This run was characterised by extreme
torque with values .reaching as high as 800 amp in places
passibly due to the use of a roller reamer . The slow ROP again
necesitatad a bit change and the decision was made to pull out at
3400m . Drilling parameters for this run were as follows WOB 36
33 klb RPM 57 6 flow 580 584 gpm and SPP of 2901 2906
psi . Only one survey was taken on this run at a depth of 3374m
having an inclination of .6 dag and an azimuth of 165.3 deg .

TELECO RUN # 11 DHB 275 10 ( 3400m 3434m )

A Seurity bit with 3 X 5 Jets replaced the Reed bit after
Drilling resumed at 3400m torque was steady at 100 160 Amps
with an average drilling rate of ! .3 meters an hour for the
lenght of this run . Drilling paramters for tnis run were as
follows WOB 28 57 KIbs RPM 73 125 Flowrate 574 590 gpm
and at standpipe pressure of 2950 psi . Due to the vary slow

TELECO RUN # 12 DHB 275 10 ( 3434m 3434m )

For this run the bottom hole was changed by putting a Roller
Reamer just afar tha bit and a Blade Stablizer above the TELECO
MWD tool . Running in to the hola at a bit depth of 3343m thea
drill string became stuck . After a Freepoint indicator was
runit decided to back off most of the string . This was dona at
the stabilizer above the TELECO tool 3 times an over shot was run
in but each tina the grapple was to large and was unable pull on
the BHA . The next attempt to get the BHA was by running in open
ended this was successfull in screwing into the fish but after
jarring on the fish for more than 30 hrs tha decision was made to

including the TELECO tool 275 10 was left in the hole at
18 : @ @ hrs Ist June 1989 . The top of the fish was at 3326.3m

4 . PRESSURE EVALUATION

Pore pressure analysis was not attempted whila drilling the 1214

hole section on Nancar # 1 The formations encountered whilst drilling
this well did not lend itself to a pore prassure analysis based on MWD
resistivity measurements applied to Eatons equation . No significant
clean shala bodies were found on which to base a normal compaction trend
line critical to any qualitative analysis .

WIR N MP N

The Teleco down hole tool tool is not a constant readout tool
hence data density i.e bed resolution of the MWD log is
dependent on data transmission speed and rate of peneraticn . As
drilling ratas increase ( higher logging speed ) the number of
data points for any depth interval decreasas as doas bed
resolution . Conversely the opposite applies a lower rate of
peneration ( slower logging speed ) will give improved bed
resolution .

Approximations of data sampling rates are :

at 3035mhr the sample rate would be two resistivities and one
gamma ray avery Q.4dm5

at 190mhr the sample rate would be two rasistivitias and one
gamma ray evary tn .

The temperaturs transmitted from tha TELECO tool and
displayed on the log is the cartridgs temperature of the MUD
tool . Results have shoun that this value is 2 dag C above that
af the mud circulating through the tool .

For a more detailed comparisons between the Teleco MWD
log and Wirelogs or any other problems ragarding use of MUD Tools
andor logs please dont hesitate to contact your nearest TELECO
office .

PP 1

The primary method usad for the pore pressure detection is Ben
Eatons pore pressure equation . The basis of the equation ls
that resistivity readings of a normally deposited shale uilt
increase with depth due to greater compaction . The method uses a
normal trend line extended throughout the well that represents
tha resistivity readings of the shales for tha entire well if
they were normally compacted . If the resistivity values in the
shales has a decreasing trend this would indicate that the shale
was becoming undercompacted and most likely over pressured .
Eatons equation is defined :

.2 Pa5 ( 5Pn ) RoRn

WHERE : P s Pore Pressure 5 s Vartable Overburden For this depth
Pns Normal Pore Pressure ( 8.68 ppg for area ) Ros Observed
Resiativity Value In Shale Rne Normal Resistivity Value In Shale

Estons equation assumas a variable overburden value which can ba
obtained by several methods . Ona mathod is to calculate
equivalent mud weight from an off set sonic log . Tha second
would be to calculate equivalent mud weights Prom the shala
dansities if available while drilling the wall . The final
method is to use the generalized overburden table calculated from
Eaton for the ares . When using the generalized overburdan tha
water depth and air gap must be added in and the overburden
recalculated since these Pactors will make a difference to the
overburden . When the various indicators for pore pressures start
to appear Eatons @ quation can be used to find the normal
resistivity value for a shale at that depth . It is assumed that
the pore pressura is equal to the mud weight and Eatons equation
then solved for the normal resistivity value .

Solve for Ron : 833 Rn e Ro ( 5P ) ( S5Pn )
Whera : Ps Pore Pressurelor MM for this casa ) 5 Variable

Overburden For This Depth Pns Normal Pore Pressurel ( 8.65 pp9 for
area ) Roz Observed Resistivity Value Rnz Normal Resistivity Value

NP MMARY

TELECOs Measurement While Drilling services were utilized aboard
the SEMISUBMERSIBLE Diamond M General for the drilling of BHP
Petroleums5s NANCAR # well and subsequent sidetrack in the Timor
Sea offshore Northern Australia . TELECOs services consist of a
gamma ray resistivity log directional surveys and related
engineering services

In NANCAR 2 13 38 casing was set at 2020m and 2 14 hole
had bean drilled to a depth of 34J4m when the BHA became stuck in
the hole while running back in after a bit trip . After trying
unsucessfully to free tha fish ( which included a TELECO MWD
tool ) the decision was made to abandon it plug back and
sidetrack in the 12 14 hole to the original planned ID of
3700nm .

The top of the cement plug was tagged at 3109m and the sidetrack
commenced with a steerable assemby . After some difficulty the
sidetrack was finally established at an inclination of about 4.8
degrees . Rotary drilling comenced at 3235m and continued to
3369m at which point it was decided to laydown TELECO since the
hole was now safely past the fish .

RILLI NG INEER

Following is an summary for each Teleco run in each section of
hole .

1214 H SECT 1

Prior to commencing the sidetrack a cement plug was seat from
303m to 3263m with the top of the fish being at 3326m . The
cement plug was set in athick consistent siltstone that had
previously drilled at about 20 mhr with a PDIC bit . Wireline
logs run before the plug was set showed that this section of hole
chosen for the kickoff was in good condition and generally less
than overgauge .

CO. RUN H t ( 3109m
The following steerable BHA was made up and run in hole :

BIT ( Hughes ATJI ! insert with 3 x 18 Jets ) DYNATRAX F2000 Combo
PDM Mud Motor XD PONY DC 12 18 STAB X0O TELECO MUD B2B71
06 ORIENTING SUB MONEL DC 12 STAB 15 x DC XO 2 x HWDP
JARS 12 x HWDP .

The top of cement was tagged at 3109m and the first few meters
wara rotary drilled to dress it At this depth the original hole
had an inclination of 9.7 deg and an azimuth of 63.2 deg .
Unfortunately the next surveys were about 100m in either
direction . The motor was oriented to approximately high side to
kickoff in the direction of the original hola and the plug was
drilled with the following parameters : 35 klbs W0OB 550 pm
and 24002500 psi SPP . ROP was about 1Q mhr until 3139m were
thara was a Br fast section ( upto 60 mhr ) presumably a bad
section of cement

Sliding continued towards high side with 8 hola azimuth about 157
deg . W0OB was gradually increased from 10 to 20 klbs as ths ROP
slowly decreased down to about 2 mhr . At times the BHA would
torque up and stop drilling until it was lifted off bottom and
reoriented . By 3169m the inclination had built very slightly
( 1.0 dag at 3150m ) but there was no evidence of any new formation
in the cuttings and ROP had slowed to ! mhr even with upto 30
klba WOB . The rasistivity and gamma ray log was very similar to
the original aection .

It was decided to POOH to change the BHA and tha bit . On surface
the bit was found to be in practically brand new condition .

TE R # 2 . HB2971 ( 3169m 33m )

The following changes were mada to the BHA . A Hughes J4 milled
tooth bit was run with 3 x 16 jets in an effort to improve the
hydraulics at the bit . A F20005 DYNATRAX was used instead of the
previous Combo type which had a long 9 58 thrust bearing
section Which was feared to be inhibiting kickoff . The upper
stabilizer was moved down one collar length to the top of the
MWD . 6 drill collara were laid down in an effort to further
improve the hydraulics .

After RIH the motor was again oriented to high side and sliding
proceeded with with following parameters : 1530 klbs W0OB 508
S40 opm and 2400 2580 psi SPP . ROP quickly decreased even
more to 0.5 mhr . Over 20m the inclination slowly increased
from . dag to 1.8 deg and the azimuth walked left from 62.9
deg to 146.7 deg . Again there was no evidence of any formation
besides cement in the cuttings . At 3193m it was decided to POOH
for a PDOC bit which was to be flown out to the rig by the time
the bit was on surface .

TELECO R HB207106 ( 3133m )

Before tha bit was on surface it was discoverad that the POCG bit
had been left behind in Darwin and s0 it was decided to rerun the
ATII used on the first run but with 3 xI6 jets this time . This
was the only change to the BHA .

After running in hole the motor was again oriented to high side
( azimuth 147 deg ? and sliding drilling commenced with 32 klbs
WOB and 590 gpm giving 28090 290d psi SPP . ROP was again
extremely slow at about 0.5 mhr . After bottonsup samples
containad a significant quantity of formation ( silty claystone )
indicating that some new hola was being drilling as was to be
expected from the inclination of 7.0 degrees .

Very slow drilling at 0.5 mhr continued until 3202m when it was
decided to POOH again so as to be on surface after the PDOC bit
finally turned up . Ona survey was taken at 3181.6m with an
inclination of 2. deg and azimuth of 149.4 dag .

On surface the insert bit was found to be hardly worn but tha
body was somewhat washed out around the teeth . The DYNATRAX
bearings wers completaly worn out with thea bit sub flush up
against the motor body and was consequently laid doun .

1 4 196 ..


After a
sucessful surface test the string was run in hole to 3088m whera
singles were washed down quickly . From 3113m singles wers rotary
reamed down to botton .

Just above bottom the motor was oriented to the hola azimuth and
drilling @ head attempted . Initial parameters were 5 10 klbs
W0B 560 gpm giving a SPP of 2000 psi when offbottom and upto
2908 psi when on bottom . Even at these low WOBs very high
erratic reactive torque was being produced by this powerful motor

m7

-----Page 282-----

and PDC bit . Toolface readings were highly erratic and very
difficult to obtain as the severe and erratic downhola twisting
of the BHA was constantly forcing the tool in and out of
nonrotating survey mode . Higher W0Bs could not be run because
they generated very high torque and consequently large mud motor
pressure drops and exceeded the rigs available pump pressure
( 3006 psi for any length of time ) .

Eventually judicous usa of low W0Bs ( 2 3 klbs ) and careful
toolface orientation produced enough toolface readings to be able
to basically keep the motor pointed in the desired direction . By
3208m the erratic torquing had decreased to an acceptable level
and toolface updates were regular and consistent . With about 5
klbs WOB ROP averaged about .5 2.5 mhr .

A survey at 3235m MD gave an inclination of 3.3 deg and azimuth
of 41. deg at 3217.7m . It was believed sufficient angle had
been built at the bottom of the hole and rotary drilling was
commenced with about 0 klbs WOB 40 RPM 560 opm and 280Q
2900 psi SPP on bottom . ROP averaged 3.5 4.5 mhr through the
same consistent siltstona . It was not possible to increase the
ROP by use of a higher W0OB because the standpipe pressure would
quickly increase bayond the rigs capacity .

By 3250m it was decided to POOH to change the BHA to a locked
rotary assembly and the bit to an insert type in preparation for
the approaching s5and sequences particulary when the PDC bit
could not be made to drill as fast as it was capable . A final
survey at 3230.6m gave an inclination of 4.7 deg and 143.2 deg
azimuth .

I R 71 K

The mud motor and POC bit were laid down and the following
packed rotary assembly was mada up ! BIT ( Security S82FEJ4 with 3
x 12 and a 4 jets ) NEAR BIT ROLLER REAMER PONY OC ( 3m ) ROLLER
REAMER X0 MUWD STABILIZER MONEL DOC 14 x DC XO 2 x HUDP
JARS 12 x HWOP .

Aftar running in hole drilling ahead proceeed with the following
parameters : 2540 klbs WOB @ 81403 RPM 540570 psi S5PP and
28003000 psi SPP . WOB and RPM wera varied in these ranges but
ROP was generally 2.5 mhr . There were occasional short ROP
breaks ( upto 5 mhr for D0.10.2m ) once the interbedded sandstones
after 3276m were reached .

Survays were taken after each single and showed that the packed
assembly was keeping the hole essentially straight . Inclination
decreased slightly from 4.8 4.4 degrees and the azimuth changed
only from 142.5 to 144.2 deg . At 3310m there was a sudden 1000
psi pressure drop due to a pump problem . Since the ROP had been
very slow it was decided to pull out at tnis change for a bit
changa .

I t 7106 ( 3310m 3369m )

Tha only changes to the BHA were the replacement of tha near bit
roller reamer with an unworn one and the usa of a REED HPSIAJ
insert bit dressed with 2 x 12s and x 6 jets . After running

in drilling ahead proceeded with the following paramatera : 30

9

-----Page 283-----

klbs WOB 90106 RPM 560 gpm and 3400 psi SPP . ROP was again
slow at 1.52.5 mhr .

Shortly after drilling ahead the resistivity data became erratic
and then the tool switched to D6 mode indicating that the tool
had detected a problem with the resistivity sensor . This
condition continued for 2.5 hrs resulting in no resistivity data
over tha interal 3300m 3368m . During this period and for many
hours afterwards there were numerous problems wih both mud
pumps . The tool returned to RGD mode after one of the numerous
times the pumps were restarted . There were no further problems
with the tool for tha rest of the run ( another 28 circulating
hours ) .

At 3328m the WOB was increased to 45 klbs and the RPM reduced to
53 with the result that the ROP increased slightly to about 2
mhr . By 3366m the ROP had decreased to about mhr and tha W0B
was further increased to 60 klbs but the ROP did not measurably
improve and at 3369m it was decided to pull out for a bit change .

Surveys were taken every connection and indicated that the hole
was holding direction and very slouly dropping angle .
Inclination decreased from 4.3 to 4.1 degrees and the azimuth
changed from 144.9 to 146.7 degrees over a course length of 57m .
The TELECO tool was laid down after this run because the bit had
now safely passed the fish and the previous saction of hole upto
3430m had already been logged . There was no advantage in wearing
out the tool or ruming the risk of losing it during the
forthcoming slow drilling in a knoun section of hole .

It was later decided not to use TELECO for the remainder of the
well due to costbenefit considerations .

4 R A N

Pore pressure analysis was not attempted uhile drilling this
124 hole section . The use of EATONs pore pressure @ quation
requires the presence of a suitably thick shala or clean
claystone that is normally pressured in order to establish a
normal pore pressure trend line . Suitable formations were not
encountered in this hole section . Most of the section drilled
consisted of very silty claystones or calcareous siltstones

Mud weight remained very constant throughout the saction at .24
1.25 56 . There was no evidence of any unusual overpressuring
from connection gas trip gas overpull or Geoservices
Dexponent plota .

BOREH RRECT LONS

Certain borehole conditions may affect the quantitative values of
nalural gamma ray and short normal resistivity values measured by
the MUD tool . These conditions : hole size mud weight mud
resistivity and bottom hole temperature sometimes require that
the measurements from the Teleco tool be corrected to mnormalize
these affects . The relationship between the collar size and the
borehole size and tha ratio of the formation to mud resistivity
( RaRm ) affect the magnitude of the correction which can be
positive or negative .

Borehale parameters for the well were monitored while drilling to
determine the amount of borehole corrections required . The mud
salinity was monitored and the temperature transmitted from the
downhole tool was usad to determina tha mud rasistivity . The
circulating temperature of the mud is approximately two deg
celsius less than that transmitted by the tool .

The 12 14 hole section was drilled with KCLPOLYPLUS mud and
had mud cehlorides of 58000 to 62000 ppm requiring 5ome
resistivity correction . This high chloride lavel tn conjunction
with downhole temperatures of upto 78 deg C result in very low
downhole mud resistivities ( 0.034 0.04 ohmm ) .

The resistivity borehole correction charts for a 8 14 tool ina
12 14 hole illustrate the care that must be exercised in
interpreting the corrected resistivity curve . A correction ratio
of 2.0 applies at RaRm sz 23 ( i.a . Raz 0.78 ohmm at Rm z 9.035
ahmm ) . This could be considered to be the limit of accurate
( i.e . quantitative ) correction . The correction ratio is 4.0
and increasing exponentially at RaRm 30 . This corresponds to
Ra 2 1.05 ohmm at the same Rm . Thesa conditions apply over much
of the 12 14 hole section .

Another important factor to be kept in mind when interpreting the
resistivity is the borehole size . At slow ROPs the resistivity
sensor may ba several hours bahind the bit . If the formation is
porous and permgable significant invasion mgy have occurred
before it is logged . If the hole is washing out the assumption
thai the hole is in gauge when it is logged may no longer be
valid . Even small washouts at high RaRm ratios render the
borehole correction factors inaccurate .

The above comments particularly apply when a sactlon is ream
logged or at tha start of a new run whan old hole is logged
before the new formation that has just heen drilled .

The following page contains the correction factors used in this
well .

6 . WIRELINE COMPARISON

The Teleco down hole tool tool is not a constant readout tool
hence data density i.e bed resolution of the MU log is
dependent on data transmission speed and rate of peneration . As
drilling rates increase ( higher logging speed ) the number of
data points for any depth interval decreases as does bed
resolution . Conversely tha opposite applies : a lower rate of
peneration ( slower logging speed ) will give improved bad
resolution .

Approximations of data sampling rates are :

at 3035mhr the sample rate would be two resistivitias and one
gamma ray every Od . 4mj

at 100mhr the sample rate would be two resistivities and ona
gamma ray every Im .

The temperature transmitted from the TELECO tool and displayed on
the log is the cartridge temparature of the MUD tool . Results
have shown that this value is 2 deg C above that of the mud
circulating through the tool .

APPENDIX I

The primary method used for the pore pressure detection is Ben
Eatons pore pressure @ quation . The basis of the equation is
that resistivity readings of a normally deposited shale will
increase with depth due to greater compaction . The method uses a
normal trend line extended throughout the wel that represents
the resistivity readings of tha shales for tha entire well if
they were normally compacted . If the resistivity values in tha
shales has a decreasing trend this would indicate that the shale
was becoming undercompacted and most likely over prassurad .
Eatons equation is defined :

U.2 Ps5 ( 5Pn ) XRaRn

WHERE : P 2 Pore Pressure 5 Variable OQverburden For this depth
Pns Normal Pore Prassure ( 8.60 ppg for area ? Roz Observed
Resistivity Valus In Shale Rnm Normal Resistivity Value In Shale

Eatons5 equation assumes a variable overburdan values which can be
obtained by several methods . One method is to calculate
equivalent mud weight from an off set sonic log . Tha second
would be to calculate equivalent mud weights from tha shala
densities if available while drilling the well . The final
method is to usa the generalized overburden table calculated from
Eaton for the area . When using the generalized overburden the
water depth and air gap musi ba added in and the overburden
recalculated since these factors will make a difference to the
overburden . Whan tha vartous indicators for pore pressure start
to appear Eatons @ quation can be used to find the normal
resistivity value for a shala at that depth . It is assumed that
the pore pressure is equal to the mud weight and Catons equation
then solved for the normal resistivity value .

Solve for Rn : .833 Rn 2 Ro ( 5P ) ( 5Pn )

Where : P Pore Pressurelor MW for this case ) 5 m Variabla
Overburden For This Depth Pne Normal Pore Pressure ( 8.65 ppg for
area ) Roz Observed Resistivity Value Rnz Normal Resistivity Value

l1 . ABSTRACT
1.1 INTRODUCTION

This report details the positioning services provided by RACAL
SURVEY AUSTRALIA LIMITED ( RSA ) for the move of the semi
submersible drilling rig DIAMOND M. GENERAL ( DMG ) onto
location NANCAR 1 in the Timor Sea off NorthWest Australia
for BHP ENGINEERING LTD. ( BHP ) .

The survey requirements and operating procedures are in
accordance with the contract agreement between RSA and BHP .

The survey vessel M.V . Mangrove Creek on permanent charter to
BHP has been fitted out with the necessary positioning
equipment to conduct such surveys on as and when required
basis . The vessel is manned by Racal personnel at all times .

The M.V.Mangrove Creek was used to deploy the transponders
carry out the acoustic calibration deploy the marker buoys
and carry out all survey work associated with this rig move .

A four transponder acoustic net was deployed and calibrated
( both relatively and absolutely ) at the Nancar 1 location
during the 2nd3rd April 1989 . The vessel was engaged in
other survey projects between the 4th13th April 1989 .

The rig was located and a final GPS position fix obtained
during the perlod 14th20th April 1989 . However the position
which had been initially supplied by BHP was amended which
meant the rig had to move some 720m on a bearing of 265 .
Therefore the acoustic net was subsequently recovered and re
deployed to provide positioning at the revised Nancar 1
location .

RACALE

-----Page 302-----

Page : 2

The acoustic net was redeployed on the 22nd April . A relative
and absolute calibrations were then performed back to back on
the same day . Marker buoys were laid and the rig was re
located . The final GPS fix was observed on the 24th April .

A Trimble 4000AX ( Global Positioning System ) receiver and the
AquaFix acoustic system used in conjunction with a HP9920
series desktop computer supported by Racals GNS26 software
was used to provide the onboard realtime navigation of the
survey vessel during the transponder deployment and calibration
and also to assist in the deployment of the marker buoys .

RACALE

-----Page 303-----

Page : 3

3 . REQUIREMENTS

BHP were to provide a Del Norte 1005 GPS receiver whilst
Racal Survey Australia Ltd. were to provide a Trimble GPS
Receiver an acoustic and computer system together with the
GNS26 Navigation and AQX Acoustic Calibration Software
Packages . The acoustic system was to consist of four AquaFix
transponders .

The survey procedure was to be as follows :

( a ) To deploy and calibrate both relatively and absolutely
( against GPS ) an array of four acoustic transponders
around the Nancar 1 location .

( b ) A combination of acoustics a and GPS would be used to
position marker buoys on the four primary anchor
locations plus two additional port and starboard gate
buoys located 100m either side of the proposed location .

( c ) To assist the anchor handling vessels in positioning the
anchors in their correct position .

( d ) To transfer an acoustic and GPS system to the rig to
monitor the rigs position during the running of the
secondary anchors pretensioning and ballasting down
stages plus the final manouevering onto the proposed
location .

( e ) To ensure that the final position of the drillstem
was within the 30 metre tolerance circle centred on the

proposed location as stated by BHP .

( f ) To confirm the acoustic position of the rig by observing
a final differential GPS fix .

5 . OPEBRATIONAL SUMMARY
5.1 TRANSPONDER DEPLOYMENT

The transponders were deployed during a period when it was
possible to track 3 or more satellites at one time with the GPS
receiver thus ensuring the best position fix . The drop
position and depth of each transponder was recorded and used
in the relative calibration . The transponders were laid in a
pattern approximately 1000 metres radius from the initial
proposed location .

The transponder array was deployed around the initial proposed
location on the 2nd April 1989 . The following transponders
being utilised :

Code SN Freq . ( kHz )
AB45 117 10.5
ABC3 . 396 14.0
AB12 187 12.0
A125 369 15.0

Following the revision of the proposed drilling location the
transponders were recovered and the following transponders
redeployed in an array around the new location :

Code SN Freq . ( kHz )
AB45 117 10.5
AB2 MAO02 11.0
AB12 187 12.0
ABC3I 396 14.0

Each of the four transponders was attached to 2 x 35kg sinkers
a 2.5m anchor strop 2 floats and a 1m lift strop . The
transponders have a transmission height of 4.0m above the
seabed .

RACALE

-----Page 310-----

Page : 10

5.2 VELOCITY PROFILE

It was not possible to use the velocimeter to determine the
speed of sound in the water column as it had been sent off for
repair . The necessary data was therefore acquired by
interrogating the temperaturesalinity sensors fitted to one of
the Aquafix 4 transponders on the 2nd April 1989 .

The transponder was lowered in 10 metre increments from the
surface to the seabed the temperature and salinity data being
relayed to the surface at each depth . The velocity propagation
was calculated for each depth . The calculation was repeated
whilst recovering the transponder to the surface .

A mean velocity of sound through the water 5 column of 1528.3
metres per second was computed when the transponder was
lowered to the seabed and a value of 1529.2 metres per second
was computed as the transponder was recovered . Using both sets
of data a mean velocity of sound through the water column of
1528.75 metres per second was derived and it is this value
that was used throughout the project .

The Wilsons equation used to calculate velocity from
temperature and salinity readings viz . :

C z 1449 # 4.6T O.055T ? 4 0.0003T9 # ( 1.39 0.012T ) Xx
( S 35 ) ft 0.017 D

where : a Velocity of sound in water

Water temperature in degrees Centigrade

Salinity of water in parts per thousand

5.3 RELATIVE CALIBRATION

On deployment of each transponder the approximate drop co
ordinates were recorded along with the water depth as recorded
by the Atlas Deso 20 echo sounder . The drop coordinates and
the depth of the transponder transmission point was entered
into the AQX software prior to commencement of the calibration .

In order to carry out the relative calibration range data from
all the transponders was acquired . This was achieved by the
survey vessel steaming within the area covered by the array and
logging all ranges received from all of the transponders . The
range data was manually selected at approximately one minute
intervals andor when the ranges from the transponders were
deemed to be stable .

Initial Nancar 1 Acoustic Net

In this initial calibration a total of 41 data sets were
logged these were then processed using the Racal Agx
relative calibration software . The output from this program
was a set of local coordinates and a set of estimated
absolute coordinates for the transponders .

This relative calibration produced the following coordinates :

5.4 AB8BOLUTE CALIBRATION

The output from the relative calibration is a set of
coordinates for the transponders that are relatively correct
however they still require to be tied into the coordinate
system being used in this case the Australian Geodetic Datun .

All the absolute calibration position data from a Trimble
40005X GPS receiver and range data from the transponders were
received and logged simultaneously ( time tagged and deskewed ) .
To ensure a nonbiased set of data data was acquired from all
areas within the acoustic array by the vessel steaming slowly
through the network ensuring that data was only logged whilst
the vessel was on a constant heading . To further enhance the
quality of the GPS data monitoring of the selected satellite
constellations was carried out from a point of known co
ordinates on Troughton Island . A set of differential
corrections was obtained for the duration of the absolute
calibration and these corrections were subsequently applied to
the logged data during the final absolute calibration
computations .

Initial Nancar 1

The initial absolute calibration was carried out between 2118
hrs . and 2246hrs . ( GMT ) on the 3rd April 1989 .

A total of 66 sets of simultaneous GPS and acoustic data were

logged of which 2 were rejected by the surveyor as not being
within the desired criteria .

5.5 GENERAL SUMMARY OF EVENTS

The transponders were deployed for the rig move to the Nancar 1
location based on the initial proposed location of the rig and
its associated anchor pattern as provided by BHP on 1st April
1989 . 5 The net was deployed and relatively calibrated on the
2nd April 1989 . Absolute calibration was carried out during
the period of satellite coverage on the following day .

During the period 4th April to 13th April the vessel was
engaged in the survey operations not necessarily concerned with
this particular rig move .

On the 14th April buoys were laid in the vicinity of the
D.M.G . to mark the existing flowlines and wellheads . The
D.M.G . recovered its anchors on the 15th April . The following
day marker buoys were laid at the Nancar 1 site to indicate
positions for the primary anchors and for the two gate buoys
either side of the proposed location .

Each marker buoy had a pennant rope long enough to allow for
tide and current and was equipped with a flag strobe light
and three pimple buoys ( which gave some indication of the
current strength ) . The position of the buoys and the direction
of the surface current was checked and monitored prior to the
rigs arrival on location . All relevant information was passed
onto the rig as required .

The rig was towed onto location on the le6th April by an anchor
handling vessel deploying anchor # 7 on the runin . The
Mangrove Creek marked the proposed drop locations as
required .

RACALE


-----Page 317-----

Page : 17

Once the primary anchors had been deployed an acoustic system
a GPS receiver and the survey personnel were transferred to the
rig . The Aquafix transducer was deployed in the moonpool and
the rig advised of its position relative to the proposed
location .

The remaining anchors had been run by 0155 hrs . on the 17th
April and by 0740 hrs . the rig was ballasted down and the
final acoustic fix was obtained . Later the same day the
surveyors and the navigation equipment were transferred back to
the Mangrove Creek as all nonessential personnel were
evacuated from the rig due to the close proximity of tropical
cyclone Orson . The marker buoys that remained intact were
recovered that afternoon .

On the 19th April the weather had abated sufficiently for the
transponders to be recovered .

The surveyors were transferred back onto the rig on the 20th
April to carry out the final GPS satellite position fix . On
completion of the latter the survey equipment and the
personnel transferred to the Mangrove Creek .

On the 21st April BHP advised the Mangrove Creek that the
proposed location had been changed and the rig needed to be
moved 720 metres on a bearing of 265 .

The transponder net was redeployed on the 22nd April and
relatively calibrated the same day . An absolute calibration
using the Del Norte GPS receiver was also completed . The
anchor and gate marker buoys were also deployed . By 1915 hrs .
the same day all the primary anchors had been deployed and
the marker buoys were recovered . The rig then shut down until
the following day .

RACALE

-----Page 318-----

Page : 18

The following day a difference of about 20 metres was noted
between the Aquafix and GPS as a check the acoustic net was
absolutely calibrated again using the Trimble GPS receiver .

on the 23rd April the surveyors GPS and Aquafix equipment
were transferred to the rig . The rig was ballasted down by
1500 hrs . and the final acoustic fix was then taken . Data
gathering for the final GPS fix commenced on the 24th April . A
power failure on the rig was thought to cause a loss of data .
However on reevaluation of the available data after the
personnel had transferred back to the Mangrove Creek it was
deemed not necessary to carry out any further satellite
observations .

Details of the final rig position can be found in sections 2
and 6 of this report .

RACAL


-----Page 319-----

Page : 19

6 . FINAL RIG POSITION

In order to avoid confusion only details of the final rig
position at the revised Nancar 1 site will be detailed in
this section of the report .

6.1 FINAL GP8 FIX
GPS observations were taken from 0510 hrs . to 0655 hrs .
( local time ) on the 24th April 1989 with differential
corrections being relayed from the monitor station on
Troughton Island via the Mangrove Creek . The computed

mean of the observations taken was as follows :

Latitude : 102 59 20.676 South
Longitude :125 ? 45 04.103 East

Eastings : 800 665.1 metres
Northings : 8 783 847.4 metres

Heading : 158 ?

This position is 30.3 metres on a bearing of 325 ? 17 from
the proposed location .

RACALE


-----Page 320-----

Page : 20

6.2 FINAL ACOUSTIC FIX

The Aquafix acoustic equipment was installed on the rig
after all the anchors had been run :

At 1505 hrs . on the 23rd April 1989 the final set of
acoustic ranges were observed and the drillstem position
accepted as being within the required tolerance . A set of
ten observations were made to the four transponders these
observations were averaged and a final position for the
drillstem was determined as being :

Latitude : 109 59 21.017 South
Longitude : 1252 45 04.567 East

Eastings : 800 679.1m
Northings : 8 783 836.8m

Heading : 158 ?

This position is 14.6 metres on a bearing of 347 ? 08 ! from
the proposed location .

The difference between the final Acoustic and GPS positions
is 18.33 metres on a bearing of 306.6 ? ( i.e . the satellite
position 1s Northwest of the acoustic position ) .

COMMISSION

0036M

COMMISSION

To verify the position of the DIAMOND M GENERAL DRILL PLATFORH whilst
on location at Nancar No.1 Well in the Timor Sea .

The method used to determine the position was by Differential range correction
using the satellite broadcast ephemeris pseudorange measurement of the
CAcode and the carrier phase .

A monitoring GPS unit was established at a known station on Troughton Island
and differential range corrections transferred to the drill platform by radio link .

-----Page 326-----

RECEIVER SITE

2 . RECEIVER SITE

The DIAMOND M GENERAL was anchored at Nancar No.1 Well . The Del Norte
1005 antenna was set up on the bridge deck .

This site was selected as the most unobstructed position for collecting data
from the satellites .

0036M 2 .

I . INTRODUCTION

A total of 12 sidewall core samples have been scrutinized for foraminifera
and calcareous nannoplankton fram the interval 2225m to 2704m in Nancar1 .
With only biostratigraphic subdivision required attention has focussed on
planktonic calcarecus microfossils and selected stratigraphically important

benthonic foraminiferal taxa .

BHP NANCAR11ST WELL

PALYNOLOGICAL REPORT

by

ROBIN HELBY and ROGER MORGAN

December 4 1989

-----Page 342-----

BASIC DATA
INTRODUCTION .

One hundred and fifteen samples comprising 53 sidewall cores
eight conventional core samples and fifty four ditch cuttings
samples from BHP Nancar1 were processed and their
palynological contents examined Microfossil recoveries were
generally moderate dropping to meagre or extremely meagre
below 3600m . The state of preservation of the palynomorphs was
generally fair . The presence or absence of selected taxa are

illustrated on Chart 1 and2

All samples were processed by Laola Pty . Limited Perth . They
report that all sidewall cores showed moderate to substantial
mud penetration . Cretaceous caving was often dominant in the
ditch cuttings samples between 32793423m and increasingly
prominent below 3590m . Kerogen slides were prepared from all
conventional core sidewall core samples and selected ditch

cuttings samples .
